[2026-01-19T03:10:05Z] Ryan Colaço: Literally, it comes from "co" +"lactus"... "With Milk" ... ↵ Basically, it referred to a "step prince"... ↵  In Portuguese royal families, if a Queen or a noblewoman couldn't nurse her own child (the Prince or Infante), a woman from a loyal, noble family was chosen as a "stepmother" to nurse the prince/princess.... The biological son of that stepmom would be raised alongside the prince/ess as a step-prince. Because they shared the same milk, they were legally and socially considered "part regent" ‎<This message was edited>
